            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable Li batteries have risen to prominence as key devices for green and sustainable energy development.  Mn- and Fe-based cathode materials, such as LiMn2O4 and LiFePO4, are used in large-scale batteries for elec. vehicles.  Mn and Fe are abundant elements in the Earth's crust, but Li is not.  In contrast to Li, Na is an attractive charge carrier from elemental abundance.  Recently, some layered materials, where Na can be electrochem. and reversibly extd./inserted, have been reported.  However, their reversible capacity is typically limited to 100 mA-h/g.  Herein, the authors report a new electrode material, P2-Na2/3[Fe1/2Mn1/2]O2, that delivers 190 mA-h/g of reversible capacity in Na cells with the electrochem. active Fe3+/Fe4+ redox.  These results will contribute to the development of rechargeable batteries from the earth-abundant elements operable at room temp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHU9moaXs6J7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liPPzVdrfzxKw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xmt1GqtL8%253D&amp;md5=519efcb60bb0a6fd4843546d51921eb7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1038/nmat2920"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Berthelot, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carlier, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Delmas, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical Investigation of the P2–Na<sub>x</sub>CoO<sub>2</sub> Phase Diagram</span>. <i>Nat.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical investigation of the P2-NaxCoO2 phase diagram</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Berthelot, R.; Carlier, D.; Delmas, C.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na layered oxides NaxCoO2 form one of the most fascinating low-dimensional and strongly correlated systems; in particular P2-NaxCoO2 exhibits various single-phase domains with different Na+/vacancy patterns depending on the Na concn.  Here the authors used Na batteries to clearly depict the P2-NaxCoO2 phase diagram for x ≥ 0.50.  By coupling the electrochem. process with an in situ x-ray diffraction expt., the authors identified the succession of single-phase or two-phase domains appearing on Na intercalation with a rather good accuracy compared with previous studies.  The authors reported new single-phase domains and the authors underlined the thermal instability of some ordered phases from an electrochem. study at various temps.  As each phase was characterized by the position of its Fermi level vs. the Na+/Na couple, the synthesis of each material, even in large amts., can be carried out electrochem.  The phys. properties of the as-prepd. Na1/2CoO2 and Na2/3CoO2 ordered phases were characterized and compared.  Electrochem. processes are an accurate route to precisely study in a continuous way such a complex system and provide a new way to synthesize materials with a very narrow existence range.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrk1JcT1P9myrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liPPzVdrfzxKw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXhsFKisrvJ&amp;md5=d9d06332c38e3009393054b672c767f7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1149/2.0151514jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Review—Practical Issues and Future Perspective for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Research on electrochem. Na intercalation in battery system has been reported since the early 1980s but Na-ion batteries are not commercialized so far though studies on Li-ion batteries have been reported since the late 1970s and the practical batteries have been extensively utilized for portable device applications in the world since 1991.  Now, targeted application of research and development for rechargeable batteries has changed toward realization of the sustainable energy society.  With the change in social situation and development of the battery technol., studies on Na-ion batteries have been attracted significant interests since 2010.  Although research interests of the electrode materials for Na-ion batteries are evoked in many researchers, advantages, disadvantages, and issues are not fully discussed for realizing the commercialization of Na-ion batteries.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot-2IKXj-Q-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhy8B19TkQqCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvF2rsbk%253D&amp;md5=cfc7b2d153696dcbded22d954ff06174</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201700463"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Muñoz-Márquez, M.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Room-temperature stationary sodium-ion batteries for large-scale electric energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Huilin; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.  However, after intensive research efforts, we believe that low-cost, long-life and room-temp. sodium-ion batteries would be promising for applications in large-scale energy storage system in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqNKJTie6WmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhy8B19TkQqCA"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1021/acsnano.9b00375</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D3666-3676%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DX.%2BOu%26author%3DL.%2BCao%26author%3DX.%2BLiang%26author%3DF.%2BZheng%26author%3DH.-S.%2BZheng%26author%3DX.%2BYang%26author%3DJ.-H.%2BWang%26author%3DC.%2BYang%26author%3DM.%2BLiu%26title%3DFabrication%2Bof%2BSnS2%252FMn2SnS4%252FCarbon%2BHeterostructures%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2Bwith%2BHigh%2BInitial%2BCoulombic%2BEfficiency%2Band%2BCycling%2BStability%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.9b00375&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b18997&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.9b00375&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fabrication of SnS2/Mn2SnS4/Carbon Heterostructures for Sodium-Ion Batteries with High Initial Coulombic Efficiency and Cycling Stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ou, Xing; Cao, Liang; Liang, Xinghui; Zheng, Fenghua; Zheng, Hong-Sheng; Yang, Xianfeng; Wang, Jeng-Han; Yang, Chenghao; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3666-3676</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnS2 has been extensive studied as an anode material for sodium storage owing to its high theor. specific capacity, whereas the unsatisfied initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) caused by the partial irreversible conversion reaction during the charge/discharge process is one of the crit. issues that hamper its practical applications.  Hence, heterostructured SnS2/Mn2SnS4/carbon nanoboxes (SMS/C NBs) have been developed by a facial wet-chem. method and utilized as the anode material of sodium ion batteries.  SMS/C NBs can deliver an initial capacity of 841.2 mAh g-1 with high ICE of 90.8%, excellent rate capability (752.3, 604.7, 570.1, 546.9, 519.7, and 488.7 mAh g-1 at the current rate of 0.1, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 5.0, and 10.0 A g-1, resp.), and long cycling stability (522.5 mAh g-1 at 5.0 A g-1 after 500 cycles).  The existence of SnS2/Mn2SnS4 heterojunctions can effectively stabilize the reaction products Sn and Na2S, greatly prevent the coarsening of nanosized Sn0, and enhance reversible conversion--alloying reaction, which play a key role in improving the ICE and extending the cycling performance.  Moreover, the heterostructured SMS coupled with the interacting carbon network provides efficient channels for electrons and Na+ diffusion, resulting in an excellent rate performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpbZ1R4cwpT7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhy8B19TkQqCA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Investigation of layer structured NbSe2 as an intercalation anode material for sodium-ion hybrid capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Subramanian, Yuvaraj; Veerasubramani, Ganesh Kumar; Park, Myung-Soo; Kim, Dong-Won</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A layer structured NbSe2 material is synthesized through gas-phase solid state reaction, and its electrochem. performance was examd. as an intercalation anode for sodium-ion hybrid capacitor.  The NbSe2 electrode showed a reversible capacity of 142.5 mAh g-1 at 200 mA g-1 over 100 cycles with good capacity retention of 94.0%, and it delivered a high discharge capacity of 100.7 mAh at 1000 mA g-1.  The surface capacitive process mainly contributed to the charge storage in the NbSe2 electrode.  Its superior electrochem. performance arose from the layered structure of NbSe2 that offered the easy pathway for sodium ion diffusion and accommodated the vol. strain during sodiation/de-sodiation processes.  The sodium-ion hybrid capacitor assembled with NbSe2 anode and activated carbon cathode exhibited a high power d. of 599.6 Wkg-1 at energy d. of 17.3 Wh kg-1 with good capacity retention of 93.2% at 300 mA g-1 after 3000 cycles.  The results demonstrate that the NbSe2 can be a promising anode material for sodium-ion hybrid capacitor.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpD-1Gk5jah_rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhy8B19TkQqCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXosVGksr4%253D&amp;md5=02a327403fccea20c3b9e44a3c4a91c4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA00003K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Progress in Layered Metal Dichalcogenide Nanostructures as Electrodes for High-Performance Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                 10.1039/C7TA00003K</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D7667-7690%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DW.%2BKang%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BXu%26title%3DRecent%2BProgress%2Bin%2BLayered%2BMetal%2BDichalcogenide%2BNanostructures%2Bas%2BElectrodes%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BSodium-ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC7TA00003K&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b18997&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC7TA00003K&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent progress in layered metal dichalcogenide nanostructures as electrodes for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kang, Wenpei; Wang, Yuyu; Xu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7667-7690</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have emerged as a promising candidate for large-scale stationary energy storage in light of possible concerns over cost and abundance.  Advanced sodium host materials are required for developing SIBs with high energy d., long cycling stability and high safety.  Layered metal dichalcogenides (MX2, M = Mo, W, Sn, V, Ti; X = S, Se, Te) have become a hot spot for anode materials in SIBs due to their merits of high cond., mech. and thermal stability and structural stability.  In this review, we first present a comprehensive overview of the progress of layered MX2 anodes for SIBs.  Detailed discussion on the advantages of MX2 as SIB anodes is then made.  Emphasis is placed on enhancing the electrochem. performance through nanostructure engineering, crystal structure modulation, doping/alloying and composite design.  We conclude with a perspective on the further development of SIBs in view of their applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqJtS76pRrKJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhM3oP7U2cIpA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXksFCksrs%253D&amp;md5=937107c9b1a2d8e6950bcbe9c948edd3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA06667A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Veerasubramani, G. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">20056</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">20068</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C8TA06667A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D20056-20068%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DG.%2BK.%2BVeerasubramani%26author%3DY.%2BSubramanian%26author%3DM.%2BS.%2BPark%26author%3DG.%2BNagaraju%26author%3DB.%2BSenthilkumar%26author%3DY.-S.%2BLee%26author%3DD.-W.%2BKim%26title%3DEnhanced%2BStorage%2BAbility%2Bby%2BUsing%2Ba%2BPorous%2BPyrrhotite%2540N-doped%2BCarbon%2BYolk-Shell%2Bstructure%2Bas%2Ban%2BAdvanced%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC8TA06667A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b18997&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC8TA06667A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced storage ability by using a porous pyrrhotite@N-doped carbon yolk-shell structure as an advanced anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Veerasubramani, Ganesh Kumar; Subramanian, Yuvaraj; Park, Myung-Soo; Nagaraju, Goli; Senthilkumar, Baskar; Lee, Yun-Sung; Kim, Dong-Won</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20056-20068</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are undoubtedly the most promising alternatives to lithium-ion batteries considering the natural abundance, distribution and cost of sodium resources.  Still, SIBs face challenges in the development of suitable anode materials due to the large vol. change during sodiation/de-sodiation, which results in inferior cycling stability.  Herein, we synthesized a yolk-shell structured pyrrhotite (Fe1-xS)@N-doped carbon (FS@NC) through a soln.-based method and investigated its electrochem. properties for use in SIBs as an anode material.  The optimized yolk-shell structured FS@NC with distinctive voids and a core exhibited a high reversible capacity of 594 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1, excellent rate capability and superior cycling performance compared to core-shell and pristine Fe1-xS materials.  During the charge and discharge cycles, the synergistic effect of the porous core (Fe1-xS) with empty voids and a defective carbon shell configuration provided a large electrode/electrolyte contact area and shortened the diffusion path for electrons and sodium ions.  It also mitigated the structural degrdn. by accommodating the vol. change during continuous cycles, which was confirmed by ex situ SEM and TEM analyses.  To demonstrate a practical application, we assembled a sodium-ion full cell with an O3-type NaCo0.5Fe0.5O2 cathode and a yolk-shell structured FS@NC anode, and the results showed superior energy storage performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoM_lzad_9x2LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhM3oP7U2cIpA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhslCju7rO&amp;md5=157071ee13d847fe836eed1c57c7d429</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1039/C7EE01100H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Paik, U.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structure-Designed Synthesis of FeS<sub>2</sub>@C Yolk-Shell Nanoboxes as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure-designed synthesis of FeS2@C yolk-shell nanoboxes as a high-performance anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Zhiming; Lu, Tianchi; Song, Taeseup; Yu, Xin-Yao; Lou, Xiong Wen; Paik, Ungyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pyrite (FeS2) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 894 mAh g-1.  However, its practical application is greatly hindered by the rapid capacity fading caused by the large vol. expansion upon sodiation.  Tuning the morphol. and structure at nanoscale and applying a higher cut-off voltage are essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile etching method coupled with a novel sulfidation-in-nanobox strategy is developed to synthesize unique FeS2@C yolk-shell nanoboxes.  The as-obtained FeS2@C nanoboxes reveal excellent sodium storage performance.  The remarkable electrochem. properties are attributed to the elaborate yolk-shell nanoarchitecture.  In particular, it delivers a high specific capacity of 511 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  Furthermore, a high specific capacity of 403 mAh g-1 even at 5 A g-1 is delivered.  Most impressively, a stable capacity of 330 mAh g-1 can still be retained at 2 A g-1 even after 800 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvJjmhFrYQyrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhM3oP7U2cIpA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXptFamsL0%253D&amp;md5=36e009c64dd7a8c52d074bf74fb945a8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1039/C5EE03262H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhancing the Cycling Stability of Na-ion Batteries by Bonding SnS<sub>2</sub> Ultrafine Nanocrystals on Amino-functionalized Graphene Hybrid Nanosheets</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improving cycle stability of SnS anode for sodium-ion batteries by limiting Sn agglomeration</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Wenhui; Shi, Liang; Lan, Danni; Li, Quan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

We show exptl. evidence of progressive Sn agglomeration and cryst. By replacing the commonly adopted acetylene black conductive additive with multi-wall carbon nanotubes (MWCNT), the cycle stability of the SnS electrode is largely improved, which correlates well with the obsd. suppression of both Sn agglomeration and Na2S enrichment at the end of de-sodiation cycle.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unraveling the Na-ion storage performance of a vertically aligned interlayer-expanded two-dimensional MoS2@C@MoS2 heterostructure</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Veerasubramani, Ganesh Kumar; Park, Myung-Soo; Nagaraju, Goli; Kim, Dong-Won</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Achieving hierarchically uniform surface manipulated nanostructured materials is important to accomplish high performance storage devices, but it is still challenging.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered SnS2-reduced graphene oxide (RGO) composite - A high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life sodium-ion battery anode material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qu, Baihua; Ma, Chuze; Ji, Ge; Xu, Chaohe; Xu, Jing; Meng, Ying Shirley; Wang, Taihong; Lee, Jim Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A SnS2-RGO composite with excellent electrochem. performance was prepd. as the anode of sodium ion batteries.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Few-Layered SnS2 on Few-Layered Reduced Graphene Oxide as Na-Ion Battery Anode with Ultralong Cycle Life and Superior Rate Capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yandong; Zhu, Peiyi; Huang, Liliang; Xie, Jian; Zhang, Shichao; Cao, Gaoshao; Zhao, Xinbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">481-489</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have been considered as promising alternatives to Li-ion batteries due to the natural abundance of sodium resources.  Searching for high-performance anode materials currently becomes a hot topic and also a great challenge for developing Na-ion batteries.  In this work, a novel hybrid anode is synthesized consisting of ultrafine, few-layered SnS2 anchored on few-layered reduced graphene oxide (rGO) by a facile solvothermal route.  The SnS2/rGO hybrid exhibits a high capacity, ultralong cycle life, and superior rate capability.  The hybrid can deliver a high charge capacity of 649 mA-h/g at 100 mA/g.  At 800 mA/g (1.8C), it can yield an initial charge capacity of 469 mA-h/g, which can be maintained at 89% and 61%, resp., after 400 and 1000 cycles.  The hybrid can also sustain a c.d. up to 12.8 A/g (≈28C) where the charge process can be completed in only 1.3 min while still delivering a charge capacity of 337 mA-h/g.  The fast and stable Na-storage ability of SnS2/rGO makes it a promising anode for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2sS3KKxaUkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhnOGQ4UvekQw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvF2ms7jI&amp;md5=173a3c027a58922c59d5633c7a05d580</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1021/nn503582c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, W. K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance by Structural Phase Transition from Two-Dimensional Hexagonal-SnS<sub>2</sub> to Orthorhombic-SnS</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">8323</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">8333</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Sodium-Ion Battery Performance by Structural Phase Transition from Two-Dimensional Hexagonal-SnS2 to Orthorhombic-SnS</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Tengfei; Pang, Wei Kong; Zhang, Chaofeng; Yang, Jianping; Chen, Zhixin; Liu, Hua Kun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8323-8333</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structural phase transitions can be used to alter the properties of a material without adding any addnl. elements and are therefore of significant technol. value.  It was found that the hexagonal-SnS2 phase can be transformed into the orthorhombic-SnS phase after an annealing step in an argon atm., and the thus transformed SnS shows enhanced sodium-ion storage performance over that of the SnS2, which is attributed to its structural advantages.  Here, we provide the first report on a SnS@graphene architecture for application as a sodium-ion battery anode, which is built from two-dimensional SnS and graphene nanosheets as complementary building blocks.  The as-prepd. SnS@graphene hybrid nanostructured composite delivers an excellent specific capacity of 940 mAh/g and impressive rate capability of 492 and 308 mAh/g after 250 cycles at the current densities of 810 and 7290 mA/g, resp.  The performance was found to be much better than those of most reported anode materials for Na-ion batteries.  On the basis of combined ex situ Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, XPS, and ex situ X-ray diffraction, the formation mechanism of SnS@graphene and the synergistic Na-storage reactions of SnS in the anode are discussed in detail.  The SnS experienced a two-structural-phase transformation mechanism (orthorhombic-SnS to cubic-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn), while the SnS2 experienced a three-structural-phase transformation mechanism (hexagonal-SnS2 to tetragonal-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn) during the sodiation process.  The lesser structural changes of SnS during the conversion are expected to lead to good structural stability and excellent cycling stability in its sodium-ion battery performance.  These results demonstrate that the SnS@graphene architecture offers unique characteristics suitable for high-performance energy storage application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWHE3xEPCjvLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhnOGQ4UvekQw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFChtbbJ&amp;md5=4542b1e918e40b9ce5bae292de5dbcf4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1039/C8RA04421J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, S.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Brock, J. D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">SnS/C Nanocomposites for High-Performance Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>RSC Adv</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">23847</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">23853</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C8RA04421J</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D8%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D23847-23853%26journal%3DRSC%2BAdv%26author%3DS.-H.%2BYu%26author%3DA.%2BJin%26author%3DX.%2BHuang%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DR.%2BHuang%26author%3DJ.%2BD.%2BBrock%26author%3DY.-E.%2BSung%26author%3DH.%2BD.%2BAbru%25C3%25B1a%26title%3DSnS%252FC%2BNanocomposites%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBattery%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC8RA04421J&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b18997&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC8RA04421J&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">SnS/C nanocomposites for high-performance sodium ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Seung-Ho; Jin, Aihua; Huang, Xin; Yang, Yao; Huang, Rong; Brock, Joel D.; Sung, Yung-Eun; Abruna, Hector D.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">23847-23853</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have been considered as one of the most promising types of batteries, beyond lithium-ion batteries, for large-scale energy storage applications.  However, their deployment hinges on the development of new anode materials, since it has been shown that many important anode materials employed in lithium ion batteries, such as graphite and silicon, are inadequate for sodium-ion batteries.  We have simply prepd. novel SnS/C nanocomposites through a top-down approach as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  Their electrochem. performance has been significantly improved when compared to bare SnS, esp. in terms of cycling stability and rate capabilities.  SnS/C nanocomposites exhibit excellent capacity retention, at various current rates, and deliver capacities as high as 400 mA h g-1 even at the high c.d. of 800 mA g-1 (2C).  Ex situ transmission electron microscopy, X-ray diffraction and operando X-ray absorption near edge structure studies have been performed in order to unravel the reaction mechanism of the SnS/C nanocomposites.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq79GXXToHq67Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhnOGQ4UvekQw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1CjtbnL&amp;md5=18eca6dc53cbf07202096894b4ddf7de</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA03893F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">16971</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">16977</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C5TA03893F</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D16971-16977%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DY.%2BC.%2BLu%26author%3DC.%2BMa%26author%3DJ.%2BAlvarado%26author%3DN.%2BDimov%26author%3DY.%2BS.%2BMeng%26author%3DS.%2BOkada%26title%3DImproved%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BTin-sulfide%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC5TA03893F&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b18997&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC5TA03893F&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improved electrochemical performance of tin-sulfide anodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Ying Ching; Ma, Chuze; Alvarado, Judith; Dimov, Nikolay; Meng, Ying Shirley; Okada, Shigeto</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">16971-16977</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to their highly reversible capacity, tin-sulfide-based materials have gained attention as potential anodes for sodium-ion and lithium-ion batteries.  Nevertheless, the performance of tin sulfide anodes is much lower than that of tin oxide anodes.  The aim of the present investigation is to improve the electrochem. performances of SnS anodes for sodium-ion batteries using conventional org. electrolytes.  Three different carbon composite anodes, SnS/reduce graphene oxide (SnS/G), SnS/reduce graphene oxide/hard carbon (SnS/G + C), and SnS/hard carbon (SnS/C), were prepd. by hot water bath synthesis followed by mech. milling.  The mechanism of the conversion and alloying reaction was investigated by TEM.  The feasibility of SnS anodes was confirmed in a full cell configuration using Na3V2(PO4)2F3 as the cathode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpQ1W-cPNnvXrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhqvwVw_T7mYw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFSksrzK&amp;md5=4f46d069778e719ea0ccd56196f54757</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201502067"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hybrid 2D-0D Graphene-VN Quantum Dots for Superior Lithium and Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D-0D Graphene-Fe3O4 Quantum Dot Hybrids as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Huan; Jia, Mengqiu; Zhu, Qizhen; Cao, Bin; Chen, Renjie; Wang, Yu; Wu, Feng; Xu, Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">26878-26885</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal oxides can be considered as appealing candidates for sodium ion battery anode materials because these low-cost materials possess high capacity and enhanced safety.  However, the practical application of these materials is usually limited by their low electronic cond. and serious vol. change during the charging-discharging process.  Herein, we report the fabrication of 3D-0D graphene-Fe3O4 quantum dot hybrids by a facile one-pot hydrothermal approach as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  Fe3O4 quantum dots with an av. size of 4.9 nm are anchored on the surface of 3D structured graphene nanosheets homogeneously.  Such unique hierarchical structure are advantageous for enlarging the electrode/electrolyte interface area and enhancing the electrochem. activity of the hybrid materials, inhibiting particle aggregation of Fe3O4 and accommodating their vol. change during the charging-discharging process as well as enabling fast diffusion of electrons and rapid transfer of electrolyte ions.  Consequently, the 3D-0D graphene-Fe3O4 quantum dot hybrids exhibit ultrahigh sodium storage capacity (525 mAh/g at 30 mA/g), outstanding cycling stability (312 mAh/g after 200 cycles at 50 mA/g) and superior rate performance (56 mAh/g at 10 A/g).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqySiZNElc5Z7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhqvwVw_T7mYw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFanu7rN&amp;md5=18e241446b270b8baeccc2c7fb9c0f0f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1186/s11671-018-2805-x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, Y.</span></span> <i>Nanoscale Res.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational Design of 3D Honeycomb-Like SnS2 Quantum Dots/rGO Composites as High-Performance Anode Materials for Lithium/Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang Yingge; Guo Yan; Wang Yange; Peng Tao; Lu Yang; Luo Rongjie; Wang Yangbo; Luo Yongsong; Zhang Yingge; Guo Yan; Wang Yange; Peng Tao; Lu Yang; Luo Rongjie; Wang Yangbo; Luo Yongsong; Liu Xianming; Kim Jang-Kyo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale research letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">389</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1931-7573</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Structure pulverization and poor electrical conductivity of metal dichalcogenides result in serious capacity decay both in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  To resolve the above problems, a combination of metal dichalcogenides with conductive scaffolds as high-performance electrode materials has aroused tremendous interest recently.  Herein, we synthesize a 3D honeycomb-like rGO anchored with SnS2 quantum dots (3D SnS2 QDs/rGO) composite via spray-drying and sulfidation.  The unique 3D-ordered honeycomb-like structure can confine the volume change of SnS2 QDs in the lithiation/delithiation and sodiation/desodiation processes, provide enough space for electrolyte reservoirs, promote the conductivity of the SnS2 QDs, and improve the electron transfer.  As a result, the 3D SnS2 QDs/rGO composite electrode delivers a high capacity and long cycling stability (862 mAh/g for LIB at 0.1 A/g after 200 cycles, 233 mAh/g for SIB at 0.5 A/g after 200 cycles).  This study provides a feasible synthesis route for preparing 3D-ordered porous networks in varied materials for the development of high-performance LIBs and SIBs in future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSDgzd_HB-JhCO2kE7krGOBfW6udTcc2eY4QNZBgjsQP7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB3crot1GksA%253D%253D&amp;md5=d9391ca67f415778b472b8591bdf6f35</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.09.151"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ran, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultra-Small Vanadium Nitride Quantum Dots Embedded in Porous Carbon as High Performance Electrode Materials for Capacitive Energy Storage</span>. <i>J.                 10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.09.151</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D333%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D61-71%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DL.%2BZhao%26author%3DK.%2BShen%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DX.%2BZhao%26author%3DY.%2BWu%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DF.%2BRan%26title%3DUltra-Small%2BVanadium%2BNitride%2BQuantum%2BDots%2BEmbedded%2Bin%2BPorous%2BCarbon%2Bas%2BHigh%2BPerformance%2BElectrode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BCapacitive%2BEnergy%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2016.09.151&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b18997&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2016.09.151&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultra-small vanadium nitride quantum dots embedded in porous carbon as high performance electrode materials for capacitive energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Yunlong; Zhao, Lei; Shen, Kuiwen; Liu, Ying; Zhao, Xiaoning; Wu, Yage; Wang, Yanqin; Ran, Fen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">333</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultra-small vanadium nitride quantum dots embedded in porous carbon (VNQDs/PC) were fabricated by a thermal treatment process of NH4VO3/C3H6N6 under nitrogen atm.  The specific capacitance of VNQDs/PC was 1008 mF cm-2 at a c.d. of 0.004 A cm-2, whereas the VN/carbon hybrid material obtained by a solid-state blending of NH4VO3 and C3H6N6 just exhibited a capacitance of 432 mF cm-2 at the same c.d.  By mediating the ratio of NH4VO3 and C3H6N6, a max. specific capacitance of 1124 mF cm-2 was achieved at a c.d. of 0.002 A cm-2 in aq. 6 mol/L KOH electrolyte with the potential range from 0 to -1.15 V when it reached 1: 7 (wt./wt.).  Addnl., sym. supercapacitor fabricated with synthesized VNQDs/PC presented a high specific capacitance of 215 mF cm-2 at 0.002 A cm-2 based on the entire cell, and exhibited a high capacitance retention of 86.6% with c.d. increased to 5 A g-1.  The VNQDs/PC neg. electrodes were combined with Ni(OH)2 pos. electrodes for the fabrication of hybrid supercapacitors.  Remarkably, at a power d. of 828.7 W kg-1, the device delivered an ultrahigh energy d. of 47.2 Wh kg-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoMlTQXoM2oZ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhqvwVw_T7mYw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xhs1ykurrJ&amp;md5=a2e0a38f52c6fe573e8f6398e3138b44</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-017-1722-0"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alshareef, H. N.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Layered SnS Sodium Ion Battery Anodes Synthesized Near Room Temperature</span>. <i>Nano Res.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4368</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4377</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered SnS sodium ion battery anodes synthesized near room temperature</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xia, Chuan; Zhang, Fan; Liang, Hanfeng; Alshareef, Husam N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4368-4377</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this report, we demonstrate a simple chem. bath deposition approach for the synthesis of layered SnS nanosheets (typically 6 nm or ∼10 layers thick) at very low temp. (40 °C).  We successfully synthesized SnS/C hybrid electrodes using a soln.-based carbon precursor coating with subsequent carbonization strategy.  Our data showed that the ultrathin carbon shell was crit. to the cycling stability of the SnS electrodes.  As a result, the as-prepd. binder-free SnS/C electrodes showed excellent performance as sodium ion battery anodes.  Specifically, the SnS/C anodes delivered a reversible capacity as high as 792 mAh·g-1 after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA·g-1.  They also had superior rate capability (431 mAh·g-1 at 3,000 mA·g-1) and stable long-term cycling performance under a high c.d. (345 mAh·g-1 after 500 cycles at 3 A·g-1).  Our approach opens up a new route to synthesize SnS-based hybrid materials at low temps. for energy storage and other applications.  Our process will be particularly useful for chalcogenide matrix materials that are sensitive to high temps. during soln. synthesis.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polydopamine Spheres as Active Templates for Convenient Synthesis of Various Nanostructures</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Jian; Yang, Liping; Lin, Meng-Fang; Ma, Jan; Lu, Xuehong; Lee, Pooi See</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, monodisperse polydopamine (PDA) spheres with tunable diams. have been synthesized through a facile and low cost method using a deionized water and alc. mixed solvent.  The PDA spheres possess surface functional groups (-OH, -NH2), exhibiting an extraordinary versatile active nature.  It is demonstrated that the PDA spheres could serve as an active template for the convenient synthesis of various nanostructures, e.g., MnO2 hollow spheres or PDA/Fe3O4 and PDA/Ag core/shell nanostructures.  No surface modification or special treatment is required for the synthesis of these nanostructures, which makes the fabrication process simple and very convenient.  The novel application of PDA/Fe3O4 spheres as fillers in nanocomposites for high-performance capacitors is demonstrated, indicating a promising practicality.  The PDA spheres provide a new general platform not only for the facile assembly of nanostructures but also a green synthetic template for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp_3Dra2mZ3MLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liYadPe1ffvZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xhs1Sjsr%252FM&amp;md5=3f018d8f33a6b995757c517f9b8d277f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1021/la0477183"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Borchert, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shevchenko, E.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Determination of Nanocrystal Sizes: A Comparison of TEM, SAXS, and XRD Studies of Highly Monodisperse CoPt3 Particles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Borchert, Holger; Shevchenko, Elena V.; Robert, Aymeric; Mekis, Ivo; Kornowski, Andreas; Gruebel, Gerhard; Weller, Horst</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Langmuir</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2005</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">One of the most fundamental tasks in nanoscience is the accurate detn. of particle sizes.  Various methods have been developed to elucidate the mean particle diam. and the std. deviation for an ensemble of nanocrystals.  However, good agreement between the results from different methods is not always encountered in the literature.  In this study, we investigate colloidally prepd., highly monodisperse CoPt3 nanoparticles by transmission electron microscopy (TEM), small-angle X-ray scattering (SAXS), and powder X-ray diffraction (XRD).  The results are compared in order to examine to which extent agreement is obtained by the different techniques when applied to small nanocrystals in the size range below 10 nm.  In particular, the applicability of the simple Scherrer formula for size detn. from the broadening of XRD reflections is checked.  When the different techniques are correctly applied, the results from all methods are in good agreement.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGolGYpcfuIBF7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liYadPe1ffvZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2MXosFWisg%253D%253D&amp;md5=72346bc0ad5c4b4a5f67f786b84b4d20</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA06106H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">S-doped Porous Carbon Confined SnS Nanospheres with Enhanced Electrochemical Performance for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">S-doped porous carbon confined SnS nanospheres with enhanced electrochemical performance for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yaping; Zhang, Yifang; Shi, Junrong; Pan, Anqiang; Jiang, Feng; Liang, Shuquan; Cao, Guozhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18286-18292</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Stannous based anode materials have been extensively studied for sodium ion batteries due to their high theor. capacities.  However, the large vol. changes upon repeated cycling always cause their structural pulverization and capacity fading.  Herein, we report the fabrication of S-doped porous hollow carbon confined SnS nanospheres particles and their good electrochem. performance as an anode material for sodium ion batteries.  Unlike previous reports, stanniferous solid carbonaceous nanospheres are novelly prepd. by a hydrothermal process, and they can be converted into yolk-shell structured Sn@C nanospheres after thermal annealing in a H2/Ar atm.  The subsequent sulfidation process can produce S-doped carbon confined SnS hollow nanospheres with high porosity.  The obtained SnS@SPC nanospheres possess a large Brunauer-Emmett-Teller (BET) surface area of 135.8 m2 g-1.  As an anode material for sodium ion batteries, the obtained yolk-shell SnS@SPC exhibits a high reversible capacity of 512 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and good cycling stability.  The void space between the carbon shell and the SnS yolk can accommodate the vol. changes during the charge/discharge process.  Meanwhile, the porous carbon shell can serve as a conductive skeleton and a reservoir for the electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrczDQvnYWhGbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liYadPe1ffvZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhs1KgtLvI&amp;md5=4045cfd829235cafa3e6b59734ae9266</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1039/C8TC05711G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sn vacancy engineering for enhancing the thermoelectric performance of two-dimensional SnS</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Heng Quan; Wang, Xiao Yang; Wu, Hong; Zhang, Bin; Xie, Dan Dan; Chen, Yong Jin; Lu, Xu; Han, Xiao Dong; Miao, Lei; Zhou, Xiao Yuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry C: Materials for Optical and Electronic Devices</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3351-3359</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The carrier type and concn. of a semiconductor are intimately assocd. with the kind and d. of point defects possessed within itself.  And two-dimensional SnS intrinsically exhibits a p-type semiconductor behavior, which is correlated with Sn vacancies.  Here, we present tuning the hole concn. of SnS in a wide range of 1016-1019 cm-3 through a cationic lattice site vacancy engineering strategy, by simply changing the molar ratio of raw materials, i.e., SnCl2 vs. Na2S·9H2O.  The thermoelec. properties of these Sn vacancy engineered SnS samples were investigated.  Combining the significantly improved power factor due to the increased hole concn. with an intrinsically low lattice thermal cond. arising from lattice anharmonicity, a respectable zT value up to 0.8 at 873 K could be achieved in polycryst. SnS.  This work demonstrates that low-cost and easily fabricated SnS is a promising candidate for thermoelec. application, despite it usually being considered as a low-asym. crystal with a relatively large band gap (∼1.1 eV).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2hNZUb_aU8rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgE5PhnmLIUVA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sn-MoS2-C@C Microspheres as a Sodium-Ion Battery Anode Material with High Capacity and Long Cycle Life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zheng, Fenghua; Pan, Qichang; Yang, Chenghao; Xiong, Xunhui; Ou, Xing; Hu, Renzong; Chen, Yu; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">23</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5051-5058</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CEUJED</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) have been regarded as a prime candidate for large-scale energy storage, and developing high performance anode materials is one of the main challenges for advanced SIBs.  Novel structured Sn-MoS2-C@C microspheres, in which Sn nanoparticles are evenly embedded in MoS2 nanosheets and a thin C film is homogeneously engineered over the microspheres, have been fabricated by the hydrothermal method.  The Sn-MoS2-C@C microspheres demonstrate an excellent Na-storage performance as an anode of SIBs and deliver a high reversible charge capacity (580.3 mA-h g-1 at 0.05 A g-1) and rate capacity (580.3, 373, 326, 285.2, and 181.9 mA-h g-1 at 0.05, 0.5, 1, 2, and 5 A g-1, resp.).  A high charge specific capacity of 245 mA-h g-1 can still be achieved after 2750 cycles at 2 A g-1, indicating an outstanding cycling performance.  The high capacity and long-term stability make Sn-MoS2-C@C composite a very promising anode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr2pkmVmxEWnrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgE5PhnmLIUVA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvFyksLg%253D&amp;md5=c45f7a7397b38fc8cfe9347283fb6d28</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA08346G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>-Covered SnS Nanosheets as Anode Material for Lithium-Ion Batteries with High Capacity and Long Cycle Life</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2-covered SnS nanosheets as anode material for lithium-ion batteries with high capacity and long cycle life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Qichang; Zheng, Fenghua; Wu, Yanan; Ou, Xing; Yang, Chenghao; Xiong, Xunhui; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">592-598</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A designed hierarchical nanostructure consisting of SnS nanosheets and ultrathin MoS2 nanosheets was achieved by a facile hydrothermal process with the assistance of fluoride and glucose.  In this unique architecture, on the one hand, SnS and MoS2 nanosheets can greatly reduce the Li-ion and electron diffusion distance in the electrode.  On the other hand, MoS2 nanosheets and amorphous carbon can not only prevent the direct exposure of SnS to the electrolyte but also maintain the structural stability of the electrode.  In addn., the MoS2 nanosheets can offer more active sites for hosting lithium ions, resulting in higher capacity.  When evaluated as anode material for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), this SnS/MoS2-C composite exhibited stable cycling performance (989.7 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 after 60 cycles), superior rate capability (675 mA h g-1 even at 5.0 A g-1) and a long cycle life (718 mA h g-1 at 2.0 A g-1 after 700 cycles).                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2/Graphene Composite Anodes with Enhanced Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Role of the Two-Dimensional Heterointerface</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Xiuqiang; Ao, Zhimin; Su, Dawei; Zhang, Jinqiang; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1393-1403</span>CODEN:
