            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene has been widely used as conformal nanobuilding blocks to improve the electrochem. performance of layered metal sulfides (MoS2, WS2, SnS, and SnS2) as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  However, it still lacks in-depth understanding of the synergistic effect between these layered sulfides and graphene, which contributes to the enhanced electroactivity for sodium-ion batteries.  Here, MoS2/reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanocomposites with intimate two-dimensional heterointerfaces are prepd. by a facile one-pot hydrothermal method.  The heterointerfacial area can be effectively tuned by changing the ratio of MoS2 to RGO.  When used as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries, the synergistic effect contributing to the enhanced reversible capacity of MoS2/RGO nanocomposites is closely related with the heterointerfacial area.  The computational results demonstrate that Na prefers to be adsorbed on MoS2 in the MoS2/RGO heterostructure rather than intercalate into the MoS2/RGO heterointerface.  Interestingly, the MoS2/RGO heterointerfaces can significantly increase the electronic cond. of MoS2, store more Na ions, while maintaining the high diffusion mobility of Na atoms on MoS2 surface and high electron transfer efficiency from Na to MoS2.  It is expected that the efforts to establish the correlation between the two-dimensional heterointerface and the electrochem. sodium-ion storage performance offer fundamental understanding for the rational design of layered metal sulfides/graphene composites as high-performance electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpB50PmkRDAvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1cofm9fvjxQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVansbY%253D&amp;md5=3d82ce10422e6d348a48b628852d1b2b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.jiec.2017.10.020"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">William, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Supercritical Ethanol Route for One-pot Synthesis of Tin Sulfide–Reduced Graphene Oxides and their Anode Performance for Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Low crystallinity SnS encapsulated in CNTs decorated and S-doped carbon nanofibers as excellent anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Shuaiguo; Zhao, Hanqing; Wang, Miao; Li, Zhong; Mi, Jie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As a charming alternative anode material for Na ion batteries (SIBs), SnS possesses outstanding theor. capacity.  However, the enormous vol. variation and intrinsic poor elec. cond. hamper its further applications.  SnS/CNTs encapsulated by S doped CNFs hybrids (SnS/CNTs@S-CNFs) were synthesized through solvothermal synthesis of SnS2/CNTs precursor, followed by electrospinning and thermal treatment.  During the thermal treatment, SnS2in-situ transformed to SnS through a phase transition process.  Simultaneously, the SnS2 dissocn. generated S atoms could dope to CNFs, which is believed to be beneficial to Na storage performance.  Thanks to the robust framework constructed by CNFs and CNTs, the as-prepd. composite can be employed as free-standing anodes for SIBs.  At a c.d. of 0.8Ag-1, a reversible capacity of 296.6 mAh g-1 can be retained after 600 cycles, corresponding to a capacity retention of 78.9%.  Besides, a superior rate capability of 252.4 mAh g-1 is achieved at 3.2 Ag-1.  Probably SnS/CNTs@S-CNFs holds great prospective as potential anode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpGoDEAJnfY67Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh1cofm9fvjxQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXpvFWrt7c%253D&amp;md5=9f61a4e2a3bfe4395281a701ee9a9650</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201500200"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kopold, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van Aken, P.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A General Strategy to Fabricate Carbon-Coated 3D Porous Interconnected Metal Sulfides: Case Study of SnS/C Nanocomposite for High-Performance Lithium and Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu Changbao; Kopold Peter; van Aken Peter A; Maier Joachim; Li Weihan; Yu Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1500200</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal sulfides have a great potential for energy storage due to the pronouncedly higher capacity (owing to conversion to metal or even alloy) than traditional insertion electrode materials.  However, the poor cycling stability still limits the development and application in lithium and sodium ion batteries.  Here, taking SnS as a model material, a novel general strategy is proposed to fabricate a 3D porous interconnected metal sulfide/carbon nanocomposite by the electrostatic spray deposition technique without adding any expensive carbonaceous materials such as graphene or carbon nanotube.  In this way, small nanorods of SnS are generated with sizes of ≈10-20 nm embedded in amorphous carbon and self-assembled into a 3D porous interconnected nanocomposite.  The SnS:C is directly deposited on the Ti foil as a current collector and neither conductive additives nor binder are needed for battery assembly.  Such electrodes exhibit a high reversible capacity, high rate capability, and long cycling stability for both lithium and sodium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSWKboLQvx6nxfKb6ELK8t0fW6udTcc2ea-G1aMtn5e17ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational Combination of an Alabandite MnS Laminated Pyrrhotite Fe1-xS Nanocomposite as a Superior Anode Material for High Performance Sodium-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Veerasubramani, Ganesh Kumar; Park, Myung-Soo; Choi, Jin-Yi; Lee, Yun-Sung; Kim, Sang Jae; Kim, Dong-Won</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Sustainable Chemistry &amp; Engineering</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Conversion-based transition metal sulfide compds. have been considered as a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  The major obstacle of these conversion-type anode materials is a large vol. change in the course of sodium-ion conversion, which deteriorates their structural stability.  Herein, we report a rational combination of pyrrhotite Fe1-xS with alabandite MnS as an anode material with the subsided structural degrdn. and improved storage ability for SIB.  Impressively, the Fe1-xS/MnS composite electrode initially delivered a discharge capacity of 602 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 with good cycling stability and excellent rate capability, which reveals its enhanced sodium-ion storage capacity as compared to its pristine electrodes (Fe1-xS, MnS).  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy and cyclic voltammetry analyses demonstrate the enhanced rate performance and improved cycling stability of the Fe1-xS/MnS composite electrode as well as better pseudocapacitive contribution.  The cooperative effect of the Fe1-xS/MnS composite anode makes it as a promising anode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq7wv8vskh__LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_KHr8DbOUQA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitVyht74%253D&amp;md5=ffd819bbc60064c23cad0c8a9b311cd8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3601"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Augustyn, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Come, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lowe, M.-A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Taberna, P.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tolbert, S.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Abruña, H.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Simon, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dunn, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-rate Electrochemical Energy Storage through Li<sup>+</sup> Intercalation Pseudocapacitance</span>. <i>Nat.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPatnkXnvsNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_KHr8DbOUQA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXlsl2jtL8%253D&amp;md5=ef16739fcf485430955b0414ac12f1ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1021/nl303305c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, S.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.-Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Microstructural Evolution of Tin Nanoparticles during In Situ Sodium Insertion and Extraction</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5897</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5902</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Microstructural Evolution of Tin Nanoparticles during In Situ Sodium Insertion and Extraction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jiang Wei; Liu, Xiao Hua; Mao, Scott X.; Huang, Jian Yu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The microstructural changes and phase transformations of tin nanoparticles during electrochem. sodiation were studied with a nanosized sodium ion battery using in situ TEM.  The first sodiation process occurred in two steps; i.e., the cryst. Sn nanoparticles were initially sodiated via a two-phase mechanism with a migrating phase boundary to form a Na-poor, amorphous NaxSn alloy (x ∼ 0.5), which was further sodiated to several Na-rich amorphous phases and finally to the crystd. Na15Sn4 (x = 3.75) via a single-phase mechanism.  The volumetric expansion was ∼60% in the first step and 420% after the second step.  However, despite the huge expansion, cracking or fracture was not obsd., which is attributed to the second step of the single-phase sodiation that accommodates large portion of the sodiation-induced stress over the entire particle.  Excellent cyclability was also obsd. during the reversible sodiation/desodiation cycles, showing great potential of Sn nanoparticles as a robust electrode material for rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4-_RnLjqf7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_KHr8DbOUQA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsFGqs7rO&amp;md5=3a9b283edadab9ac6dda7ef5c8bd18b7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b01984"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alvarado, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Somerville, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, Y.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Investigating the Energy Storage Mechanism of SnS<sub>2</sub>-rGO Composite Anode for Advanced Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>27</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5633</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5640</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b01984</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D27%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D5633-5640%26journal%3DChem.%2BMater.%26author%3DC.%2BMa%26author%3DJ.%2BXu%26author%3DJ.%2BAlvarado%26author%3DB.%2BQu%26author%3DJ.%2BSomerville%26author%3DJ.-Y.%2BLee%26author%3DY.-S.%2BMeng%26title%3DInvestigating%2Bthe%2BEnergy%2BStorage%2BMechanism%2Bof%2BSnS2-rGO%2BComposite%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BAdvanced%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.chemmater.5b01984&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b18997&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.chemmater.5b01984&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Investigating the Energy Storage Mechanism of SnS2-rGO Composite Anode for Advanced Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Chuze; Xu, Jing; Alvarado, Judith; Qu, Baihua; Somerville, James; Lee, Jim Yang; Meng, Ying Shirley</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5633-5640</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin sulfide-reduced graphene oxide (SnS2-rGO) composite material is investigated as an advanced anode material for Na-ion batteries.  It can deliver a reversible capacity of 630 mAh g-1 with negligible capacity loss and exhibits superb rate performance.  Here, the energy storage mechanism of this SnS2-rGO anode and the crit. mechanistic role of rGO will be revealed in detail.  A synergistic mechanism involving conversion and alloying reactions is proposed based on our synchrotron X-ray diffraction (SXRD) and in situ X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS) results.  Contrary to what has been proposed in the literature, we detd. that Na2S2 forms instead of Na2S at the fully discharge state.  The as-formed Na2S2 works as a matrix to relieve the strain from the huge vol. expansion of the Na-Sn alloy reaction, shown in the high resoln. transmission electron microscope (HRTEM).  In addn., the Raman spectra results suggest that the rGO not only assists the material to have better electrochem. performance by preventing particle agglomeration of the active material but also coordinates with Na-ions through electrostatic interaction during the first cycle.  The unique reaction mechanism in SnS2-rGO offers a well-balanced approach for sodium storage to deliver high capacity, long-cycle life, and superior rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoQ0HQeDv131bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg_KHr8DbOUQA"> &gt;&gt; are the COUNTER-compliant sum of full text article downloads since November 2008 (both PDF and HTML) across all institutions and individuals.                         rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A scalable and flexible hybrid energy storage system design and implementation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Younghyun; Koh, Jason; Xie, Qing; Wang, Yanzhi; Chang, Naehyuck; Pedram, Massoud</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy storage systems (ESS) are becoming one of the most important components that noticeably change overall system performance in various applications, ranging from the power grid infrastructure to elec. vehicles and portable electronics.  However, a homogeneous ESS is subject to limited characteristics in terms of cost, efficiency, and lifetime, by the energy storage technol. that comprises the ESS.  On the other hand, hybrid ESS (HESS) are a viable soln. for a practical ESS with currently available technologies as they have potential to overcome such limitations by exploiting only advantages of heterogeneous energy storage technologies while hiding their drawbacks.  However, the HESS concept basically mandates sophisticated design and control to actually make the benefits happen.  The HESS architecture should be able to provide controllability of many parts, which are often fixed in homogeneous ESS, and novel management policies should be able to utilize the control features.  This paper introduces a complete design practice of a HESS prototype to demonstrate scalability, flexibility, and energy efficiency.  It is composed of three heterogeneous energy storage elements: lead-acid batteries, lithium-ion batteries, and supercapacitors.  We demonstrate a novel system control methodol. and enhanced energy efficiency through this design practice.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr0JsM1Kx-no7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhIMwrg8g3YTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXisFekuro%253D&amp;md5=6118a2715d543225c6c57725a48080e3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1126/science.1212741"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dunn, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kamath, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tarascon, J.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrical Energy Storage for the Grid: A Battery of Choices</span>. <i>Science</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>334</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">928</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">935</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

In contrast to Li, Na is an attractive charge carrier from elemental abundance.  Recently, some layered materials, where Na can be electrochem. and reversibly extd./inserted, have been reported. Here the authors used Na batteries to clearly depict the P2-NaxCoO2 phase diagram for x ≥ 0.50.  By coupling the electrochem. process with an in situ x-ray diffraction expt., the authors identified the succession of single-phase or two-phase domains appearing on Na intercalation with a rather good accuracy compared with previous studies.  The authors reported new single-phase domains and the authors underlined the thermal instability of some ordered phases from an electrochem. study at various temps.                         rightTab-cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot-2IKXj-Q-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-QTxa0Frmrg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvF2rsbk%253D&amp;md5=cfc7b2d153696dcbded22d954ff06174</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201700463"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Muñoz-Márquez, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.  However, after intensive research efforts, we believe that low-cost, long-life and room-temp. sodium-ion batteries would be promising for applications in large-scale energy storage system in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqNKJTie6WmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-QTxa0Frmrg"> &gt;&gt;             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnS2 has been extensive studied as an anode material for sodium storage owing to its high theor. specific capacity, whereas the unsatisfied initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) caused by the partial irreversible conversion reaction during the charge/discharge process is one of the crit. issues that hamper its practical applications.  Hence, heterostructured SnS2/Mn2SnS4/carbon nanoboxes (SMS/C NBs) have been developed by a facial wet-chem. method and utilized as the anode material of sodium ion batteries.  SMS/C NBs can deliver an initial capacity of 841.2 mAh g-1 with high ICE of 90.8%, excellent rate capability (752.3, 604.7, 570.1, 546.9, 519.7, and 488.7 mAh g-1 at the current rate of 0.1, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 5.0, and 10.0 A g-1, resp.), and long cycling stability (522.5 mAh g-1 at 5.0 A g-1 after 500 cycles).  The existence of SnS2/Mn2SnS4 heterojunctions can effectively stabilize the reaction products Sn and Na2S, greatly prevent the coarsening of nanosized Sn0, and enhance reversible conversion--alloying reaction, which play a key role in improving the ICE and extending the cycling performance.  Moreover, the heterostructured SMS coupled with the interacting carbon network provides efficient channels for electrons and Na+ diffusion, resulting in an excellent rate performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpbZ1R4cwpT7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-QTxa0Frmrg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXjsVaqu7Y%253D&amp;md5=4575ad64469267af9d8a39c2100599e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201807971"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, H.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Heterostructured Nanocube-Shaped Binary Sulfide (SnCo)S<sub>2</sub> Interlaced with S-Doped Graphene as a High-Performance Anode for Advanced Na<sup>+</sup> Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Investigation of layer structured NbSe2 as an intercalation anode material for sodium-ion hybrid capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Subramanian, Yuvaraj; Veerasubramani, Ganesh Kumar; Park, Myung-Soo; Kim, Dong-Won</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A layer structured NbSe2 material is synthesized through gas-phase solid state reaction, and its electrochem. performance was examd. as an intercalation anode for sodium-ion hybrid capacitor.  The NbSe2 electrode showed a reversible capacity of 142.5 mAh g-1 at 200 mA g-1 over 100 cycles with good capacity retention of 94.0%, and it delivered a high discharge capacity of 100.7 mAh at 1000 mA g-1.  The surface capacitive process mainly contributed to the charge storage in the NbSe2 electrode.  Its superior electrochem. performance arose from the layered structure of NbSe2 that offered the easy pathway for sodium ion diffusion and accommodated the vol. strain during sodiation/de-sodiation processes.  The sodium-ion hybrid capacitor assembled with NbSe2 anode and activated carbon cathode exhibited a high power d. of 599.6 Wkg-1 at energy d. of 17.3 Wh kg-1 with good capacity retention of 93.2% at 300 mA g-1 after 3000 cycles.  The results demonstrate that the NbSe2 can be a promising anode material for sodium-ion hybrid capacitor.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpD-1Gk5jah_rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhpdU_cxM6x4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXosVGksr4%253D&amp;md5=02a327403fccea20c3b9e44a3c4a91c4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA00003K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Progress in Layered Metal Dichalcogenide Nanostructures as Electrodes for High-Performance Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">7667</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">7690</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent progress in layered metal dichalcogenide nanostructures as electrodes for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kang, Wenpei; Wang, Yuyu; Xu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have emerged as a promising candidate for large-scale stationary energy storage in light of possible concerns over cost and abundance.  Advanced sodium host materials are required for developing SIBs with high energy d., long cycling stability and high safety.  Layered metal dichalcogenides (MX2, M = Mo, W, Sn, V, Ti; X = S, Se, Te) have become a hot spot for anode materials in SIBs due to their merits of high cond., mech. and thermal stability and structural stability.  In this review, we first present a comprehensive overview of the progress of layered MX2 anodes for SIBs.  Detailed discussion on the advantages of MX2 as SIB anodes is then made.  Emphasis is placed on enhancing the electrochem. performance through nanostructure engineering, crystal structure modulation, doping/alloying and composite design.  We conclude with a perspective on the further development of SIBs in view of their applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqJtS76pRrKJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhpdU_cxM6x4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXksFCksrs%253D&amp;md5=937107c9b1a2d8e6950bcbe9c948edd3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref17" class="rightTabRefNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit17" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA06667A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Veerasubramani, G.                         rightTab-cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced storage ability by using a porous pyrrhotite@N-doped carbon yolk-shell structure as an advanced anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Veerasubramani, Ganesh Kumar; Subramanian, Yuvaraj; Park, Myung-Soo; Nagaraju, Goli; Senthilkumar, Baskar; Lee, Yun-Sung; Kim, Dong-Won</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are undoubtedly the most promising alternatives to lithium-ion batteries considering the natural abundance, distribution and cost of sodium resources.  Still, SIBs face challenges in the development of suitable anode materials due to the large vol. change during sodiation/de-sodiation, which results in inferior cycling stability.  Herein, we synthesized a yolk-shell structured pyrrhotite (Fe1-xS)@N-doped carbon (FS@NC) through a soln.-based method and investigated its electrochem. properties for use in SIBs as an anode material.  The optimized yolk-shell structured FS@NC with distinctive voids and a core exhibited a high reversible capacity of 594 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1, excellent rate capability and superior cycling performance compared to core-shell and pristine Fe1-xS materials.  During the charge and discharge cycles, the synergistic effect of the porous core (Fe1-xS) with empty voids and a defective carbon shell configuration provided a large electrode/electrolyte contact area and shortened the diffusion path for electrons and sodium ions.  It also mitigated the structural degrdn. by accommodating the vol. change during continuous cycles, which was confirmed by ex situ SEM and TEM analyses.  To demonstrate a practical application, we assembled a sodium-ion full cell with an O3-type NaCo0.5Fe0.5O2 cathode and a yolk-shell structured FS@NC anode, and the results showed superior energy storage performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoM_lzad_9x2LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhpdU_cxM6x4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhslCju7rO&amp;md5=157071ee13d847fe836eed1c57c7d429</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1039/C7EE01100H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Paik, U.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structure-Designed Synthesis of FeS<sub>2</sub>@C Yolk-Shell Nanoboxes as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Pyrite (FeS2) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 894 mAh g-1.  However, its practical application is greatly hindered by the rapid capacity fading caused by the large vol. expansion upon sodiation.  Tuning the morphol. and structure at nanoscale and applying a higher cut-off voltage are essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile etching method coupled with a novel sulfidation-in-nanobox strategy is developed to synthesize unique FeS2@C yolk-shell nanoboxes.  The as-obtained FeS2@C nanoboxes reveal excellent sodium storage performance.  The remarkable electrochem. properties are attributed to the elaborate yolk-shell nanoarchitecture.  In particular, it delivers a high specific capacity of 511 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  Furthermore, a high specific capacity of 403 mAh g-1 even at 5 A g-1 is delivered.  Most impressively, a stable capacity of 330 mAh g-1 can still be retained at 2 A g-1 even after 800 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvJjmhFrYQyrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhpdU_cxM6x4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXptFamsL0%253D&amp;md5=36e009c64dd7a8c52d074bf74fb945a8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1039/C5EE03262H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhancing the Cycling Stability of Na-ion Batteries by Bonding SnS<sub>2</sub> Ultrafine Nanocrystals on Amino-functionalized Graphene Hybrid Nanosheets</span>. <i>Energy Environ.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Flower-like SnS nanostructures are obtained by a simple solvothermal method for anode applications in Na-ion batteries.  We show exptl. evidence of progressive Sn agglomeration and cryst. Na2S enrichment at the end of de-sodiation process of the SnS electrode, both of which contribute to the capacity decay of the electrode upon repeated cycles.  By replacing the commonly adopted acetylene black conductive additive with multi-wall carbon nanotubes (MWCNT), the cycle stability of the SnS electrode is largely improved, which correlates well with the obsd. suppression of both Sn agglomeration and Na2S enrichment at the end of de-sodiation cycle.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Achieving hierarchically uniform surface manipulated nanostructured materials is important to accomplish high performance storage devices, but it is still challenging.                         rightTab-cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Few-Layered SnS2 on Few-Layered Reduced Graphene Oxide as Na-Ion Battery Anode with Ultralong Cycle Life and Superior Rate Capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yandong; Zhu, Peiyi; Huang, Liliang; Xie, Jian; Zhang, Shichao; Cao, Gaoshao; Zhao, Xinbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have been considered as promising alternatives to Li-ion batteries due to the natural abundance of sodium resources.  Searching for high-performance anode materials currently becomes a hot topic and also a great challenge for developing Na-ion batteries.  In this work, a novel hybrid anode is synthesized consisting of ultrafine, few-layered SnS2 anchored on few-layered reduced graphene oxide (rGO) by a facile solvothermal route.  The SnS2/rGO hybrid exhibits a high capacity, ultralong cycle life, and superior rate capability.  The hybrid can deliver a high charge capacity of 649 mA-h/g at 100 mA/g.  At 800 mA/g (1.8C), it can yield an initial charge capacity of 469 mA-h/g, which can be maintained at 89% and 61%, resp., after 400 and 1000 cycles.  The hybrid can also sustain a c.d. up to 12.8 A/g (≈28C) where the charge process can be completed in only 1.3 min while still delivering a charge capacity of 337 mA-h/g.  The fast and stable Na-storage ability of SnS2/rGO makes it a promising anode for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2sS3KKxaUkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgpB6RRkiaBpg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvF2ms7jI&amp;md5=173a3c027a58922c59d5633c7a05d580</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1021/nn503582c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, W.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structural phase transitions can be used to alter the properties of a material without adding any addnl. elements and are therefore of significant technol. value.  It was found that the hexagonal-SnS2 phase can be transformed into the orthorhombic-SnS phase after an annealing step in an argon atm., and the thus transformed SnS shows enhanced sodium-ion storage performance over that of the SnS2, which is attributed to its structural advantages.  Here, we provide the first report on a SnS@graphene architecture for application as a sodium-ion battery anode, which is built from two-dimensional SnS and graphene nanosheets as complementary building blocks.  The as-prepd. SnS@graphene hybrid nanostructured composite delivers an excellent specific capacity of 940 mAh/g and impressive rate capability of 492 and 308 mAh/g after 250 cycles at the current densities of 810 and 7290 mA/g, resp.  The performance was found to be much better than those of most reported anode materials for Na-ion batteries.  On the basis of combined ex situ Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, XPS, and ex situ X-ray diffraction, the formation mechanism of SnS@graphene and the synergistic Na-storage reactions of SnS in the anode are discussed in detail.  The SnS experienced a two-structural-phase transformation mechanism (orthorhombic-SnS to cubic-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn), while the SnS2 experienced a three-structural-phase transformation mechanism (hexagonal-SnS2 to tetragonal-Sn to orthorhombic-Na3.75Sn) during the sodiation process.  The lesser structural changes of SnS during the conversion are expected to lead to good structural stability and excellent cycling stability in its sodium-ion battery performance.  These results demonstrate that the SnS@graphene architecture offers unique characteristics suitable for high-performance energy storage application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWHE3xEPCjvLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgpB6RRkiaBpg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFChtbbJ&amp;md5=4542b1e918e40b9ce5bae292de5dbcf4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref26" class="rightTabRefNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit26" data-doi="10.1039/C8RA04421J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, S.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Brock, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal oxides can be considered as appealing candidates for sodium ion battery anode materials because these low-cost materials possess high capacity and enhanced safety.  However, the practical application of these materials is usually limited by their low electronic cond. and serious vol. change during the charging-discharging process.  Herein, we report the fabrication of 3D-0D graphene-Fe3O4 quantum dot hybrids by a facile one-pot hydrothermal approach as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  Fe3O4 quantum dots with an av. size of 4.9 nm are anchored on the surface of 3D structured graphene nanosheets homogeneously.  Such unique hierarchical structure are advantageous for enlarging the electrode/electrolyte interface area and enhancing the electrochem. activity of the hybrid materials, inhibiting particle aggregation of Fe3O4 and accommodating their vol. change during the charging-discharging process as well as enabling fast diffusion of electrons and rapid transfer of electrolyte ions.  Consequently, the 3D-0D graphene-Fe3O4 quantum dot hybrids exhibit ultrahigh sodium storage capacity (525 mAh/g at 30 mA/g), outstanding cycling stability (312 mAh/g after 200 cycles at 50 mA/g) and superior rate performance (56 mAh/g at 10 A/g).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqySiZNElc5Z7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgpB6RRkiaBpg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFanu7rN&amp;md5=18e241446b270b8baeccc2c7fb9c0f0f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1186/s11671-018-2805-x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, Y.</span></span> <i>Nanoscale Res.         ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1931-7573</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Structure pulverization and poor electrical conductivity of metal dichalcogenides result in serious capacity decay both in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  To resolve the above problems, a combination of metal dichalcogenides with conductive scaffolds as high-performance electrode materials has aroused tremendous interest recently.  Herein, we synthesize a 3D honeycomb-like rGO anchored with SnS2 quantum dots (3D SnS2 QDs/rGO) composite via spray-drying and sulfidation.  The unique 3D-ordered honeycomb-like structure can confine the volume change of SnS2 QDs in the lithiation/delithiation and sodiation/desodiation processes, provide enough space for electrolyte reservoirs, promote the conductivity of the SnS2 QDs, and improve the electron transfer.  As a result, the 3D SnS2 QDs/rGO composite electrode delivers a high capacity and long cycling stability (862 mAh/g for LIB at 0.1 A/g after 200 cycles, 233 mAh/g for SIB at 0.5 A/g after 200 cycles).  This study provides a feasible synthesis route for preparing 3D-ordered porous networks in varied materials for the development of high-performance LIBs and SIBs in future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSDgzd_HB-JhCO2kE7krGOBfW6udTcc2eb3VXqXcs9Karntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BB3crot1GksA%253D%253D&amp;md5=d9391ca67f415778b472b8591bdf6f35</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.09.151"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ran, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultra-Small Vanadium Nitride Quantum Dots Embedded in Porous Carbon as High Performance Electrode Materials for Capacitive Energy Storage</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultra-small vanadium nitride quantum dots embedded in porous carbon (VNQDs/PC) were fabricated by a thermal treatment process of NH4VO3/C3H6N6 under nitrogen atm.  The specific capacitance of VNQDs/PC was 1008 mF cm-2 at a c.d. of 0.004 A cm-2, whereas the VN/carbon hybrid material obtained by a solid-state blending of NH4VO3 and C3H6N6 just exhibited a capacitance of 432 mF cm-2 at the same c.d.  By mediating the ratio of NH4VO3 and C3H6N6, a max. specific capacitance of 1124 mF cm-2 was achieved at a c.d. of 0.002 A cm-2 in aq. 6 mol/L KOH electrolyte with the potential range from 0 to -1.15 V when it reached 1: 7 (wt./wt.).  Addnl., sym. supercapacitor fabricated with synthesized VNQDs/PC presented a high specific capacitance of 215 mF cm-2 at 0.002 A cm-2 based on the entire cell, and exhibited a high capacitance retention of 86.6% with c.d. increased to 5 A g-1.  The VNQDs/PC neg. electrodes were combined with Ni(OH)2 pos. electrodes for the fabrication of hybrid supercapacitors.  Remarkably, at a power d. of 828.7 W kg-1, the device delivered an ultrahigh energy d. of 47.2 Wh kg-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoMlTQXoM2oZ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCH-XVIeCwvg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xhs1ykurrJ&amp;md5=a2e0a38f52c6fe573e8f6398e3138b44</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-017-1722-0"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alshareef, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, monodisperse polydopamine (PDA) spheres with tunable diams. have been synthesized through a facile and low cost method using a deionized water and alc. mixed solvent.  The PDA spheres possess surface functional groups (-OH, -NH2), exhibiting an extraordinary versatile active nature.  It is demonstrated that the PDA spheres could serve as an active template for the convenient synthesis of various nanostructures, e.g., MnO2 hollow spheres or PDA/Fe3O4 and PDA/Ag core/shell nanostructures.         </div><div class="casAbstract">One of the most fundamental tasks in nanoscience is the accurate detn. of particle sizes.  Various methods have been developed to elucidate the mean particle diam. and the std. deviation for an ensemble of nanocrystals.  However, good agreement between the results from different methods is not always encountered in the literature.  In this study, we investigate colloidally prepd., highly monodisperse CoPt3 nanoparticles by transmission electron microscopy (TEM), small-angle X-ray scattering (SAXS), and powder X-ray diffraction (XRD).  The results are compared in order to examine to which extent agreement is obtained by the different techniques when applied to small nanocrystals in the size range below 10 nm.  In particular, the applicability of the simple Scherrer formula for size detn. from the broadening of XRD reflections is checked.  When the different techniques are correctly applied, the results from all methods are in good agreement.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGolGYpcfuIBF7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCH-XVIeCwvg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2MXosFWisg%253D%253D&amp;md5=72346bc0ad5c4b4a5f67f786b84b4d20</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref37" class="rightTabRefNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit37" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA06106H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">S-doped Porous Carbon Confined SnS Nanospheres with Enhanced Electrochemical Performance for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         rightTab-cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">S-doped porous carbon confined SnS nanospheres with enhanced electrochemical performance for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yaping; Zhang, Yifang; Shi, Junrong; Pan, Anqiang; Jiang, Feng; Liang, Shuquan; Cao, Guozhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Stannous based anode materials have been extensively studied for sodium ion batteries due to their high theor. capacities.  However, the large vol. changes upon repeated cycling always cause their structural pulverization and capacity fading.  Herein, we report the fabrication of S-doped porous hollow carbon confined SnS nanospheres particles and their good electrochem. performance as an anode material for sodium ion batteries.  Unlike previous reports, stanniferous solid carbonaceous nanospheres are novelly prepd. by a hydrothermal process, and they can be converted into yolk-shell structured Sn@C nanospheres after thermal annealing in a H2/Ar atm.  The subsequent sulfidation process can produce S-doped carbon confined SnS hollow nanospheres with high porosity.  The obtained SnS@SPC nanospheres possess a large Brunauer-Emmett-Teller (BET) surface area of 135.8 m2 g-1.  As an anode material for sodium ion batteries, the obtained yolk-shell SnS@SPC exhibits a high reversible capacity of 512 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and good cycling stability.  The void space between the carbon shell and the SnS yolk can accommodate the vol. changes during the charge/discharge process.  Meanwhile, the porous carbon shell can serve as a conductive skeleton and a reservoir for the electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrczDQvnYWhGbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljcIXIemHieFw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhs1KgtLvI&amp;md5=4045cfd829235cafa3e6b59734ae9266</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1039/C8TC05711G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The carrier type and concn. of a semiconductor are intimately assocd. with the kind and d. of point defects possessed within itself.  And two-dimensional SnS intrinsically exhibits a p-type semiconductor behavior, which is correlated with Sn vacancies.  Here, we present tuning the hole concn. of SnS in a wide range of 1016-1019 cm-3 through a cationic lattice site vacancy engineering strategy, by simply changing the molar ratio of raw materials, i.e., SnCl2 vs. Na2S·9H2O.  The thermoelec. properties of these Sn vacancy engineered SnS samples were investigated.  Combining the significantly improved power factor due to the increased hole concn. with an intrinsically low lattice thermal cond. arising from lattice anharmonicity, a respectable zT value up to 0.8 at 873 K could be achieved in polycryst. SnS.  This work demonstrates that low-cost and easily fabricated SnS is a promising candidate for thermoelec. application, despite it usually being considered as a low-asym. crystal with a relatively large band gap (∼1.1 eV).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2hNZUb_aU8rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljcIXIemHieFw"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) have been regarded as a prime candidate for large-scale energy storage, and developing high performance anode materials is one of the main challenges for advanced SIBs.  Novel structured Sn-MoS2-C@C microspheres, in which Sn nanoparticles are evenly embedded in MoS2 nanosheets and a thin C film is homogeneously engineered over the microspheres, have been fabricated by the hydrothermal method.  The Sn-MoS2-C@C microspheres demonstrate an excellent Na-storage performance as an anode of SIBs and deliver a high reversible charge capacity (580.3 mA-h g-1 at 0.05 A g-1) and rate capacity (580.3, 373, 326, 285.2, and 181.9 mA-h g-1 at 0.05, 0.5, 1, 2, and 5 A g-1, resp.).  A high charge specific capacity of 245 mA-h g-1 can still be achieved after 2750 cycles at 2 A g-1, indicating an outstanding cycling performance.  The high capacity and long-term stability make Sn-MoS2-C@C composite a very promising anode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr2pkmVmxEWnrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljcIXIemHieFw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvFyksLg%253D&amp;md5=c45f7a7397b38fc8cfe9347283fb6d28</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref43" class="rightTabRefNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit43" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA08346G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>-Covered SnS Nanosheets as Anode Material for Lithium-Ion Batteries with High Capacity and Long Cycle Life</span>. <i>J.                         rightTab-cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2-covered SnS nanosheets as anode material for lithium-ion batteries with high capacity and long cycle life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Qichang; Zheng, Fenghua; Wu, Yanan; Ou, Xing; Yang, Chenghao; Xiong, Xunhui; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A designed hierarchical nanostructure consisting of SnS nanosheets and ultrathin MoS2 nanosheets was achieved by a facile hydrothermal process with the assistance of fluoride and glucose.  In this unique architecture, on the one hand, SnS and MoS2 nanosheets can greatly reduce the Li-ion and electron diffusion distance in the electrode.  On the other hand, MoS2 nanosheets and amorphous carbon can not only prevent the direct exposure of SnS to the electrolyte but also maintain the structural stability of the electrode.  In addn., the MoS2 nanosheets can offer more active sites for hosting lithium ions, resulting in higher capacity.  When evaluated as anode material for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), this SnS/MoS2-C composite exhibited stable cycling performance (989.7 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 after 60 cycles), superior rate capability (675 mA h g-1 even at 5.0 A g-1) and a long cycle life (718 mA h g-1 at 2.0 A g-1 after 700 cycles).                         rightTab-cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2/Graphene Composite Anodes with Enhanced Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Role of the Two-Dimensional Heterointerface</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Xiuqiang; Ao, Zhimin; Su, Dawei; Zhang, Jinqiang; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene has been widely used as conformal nanobuilding blocks to improve the electrochem. performance of layered metal sulfides (MoS2, WS2, SnS, and SnS2) as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  However, it still lacks in-depth understanding of the synergistic effect between these layered sulfides and graphene, which contributes to the enhanced electroactivity for sodium-ion batteries.  Here, MoS2/reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanocomposites with intimate two-dimensional heterointerfaces are prepd. by a facile one-pot hydrothermal method.  The heterointerfacial area can be effectively tuned by changing the ratio of MoS2 to RGO.  When used as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries, the synergistic effect contributing to the enhanced reversible capacity of MoS2/RGO nanocomposites is closely related with the heterointerfacial area.  The computational results demonstrate that Na prefers to be adsorbed on MoS2 in the MoS2/RGO heterostructure rather than intercalate into the MoS2/RGO heterointerface.  Interestingly, the MoS2/RGO heterointerfaces can significantly increase the electronic cond. of MoS2, store more Na ions, while maintaining the high diffusion mobility of Na atoms on MoS2 surface and high electron transfer efficiency from Na to MoS2.  It is expected that the efforts to establish the correlation between the two-dimensional heterointerface and the electrochem. sodium-ion storage performance offer fundamental understanding for the rational design of layered metal sulfides/graphene composites as high-performance electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpB50PmkRDAvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljcIXIemHieFw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVansbY%253D&amp;md5=3d82ce10422e6d348a48b628852d1b2b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref45" class="rightTabRefNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.jiec.2017.10.020"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">William, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Supercritical Ethanol Route for One-pot Synthesis of Tin Sulfide–Reduced Graphene Oxides and their Anode Performance for Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. However, the poor cycling stability still limits the development and application in lithium and sodium ion batteries.
